href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Edinburgh Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>EDI</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGPH</b>) is an airport located in the <a href="/wiki/Ingliston" title="Ingliston">Ingliston</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, Scotland. It was the busiest airport in Scotland in 2019, handling over 14.7&#160;million passengers. It was also the <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_total_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in the United Kingdom by total passenger traffic">sixth-busiest airport in the United Kingdom</a> by total passengers in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-edinburghairport.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edinburghairport.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It is located 5&#160;<a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">NM</a> (9.3&#160;km; 5.8&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> west of the city centre, just off the <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M8 motorway (Scotland)">M8</a> and <a href="/wiki/M9_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M9 motorway (Scotland)">M9</a> motorways. It is owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Global_Infrastructure_Partners" title="Global Infrastructure Partners">Global Infrastructure Partners</a>, who are also a minority shareholder of <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The airport has one runway and one passenger terminal, and employs about 2,500 people.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Early_years"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Early years</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Access_and_ground_transport"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Access and ground transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Tram"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Tram</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Accidents_and_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Notes"><span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Turnhouse Aerodrome</i> was the most northerly British air defence base in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> used by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">Royal Flying Corps</a>. The small base opened in 1916<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and it was used to house the <a href="/wiki/No._603_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 603 Squadron RAF">603 (City of Edinburgh) Squadron</a> from 1925, which consisted of <a href="/wiki/Airco_DH.9" title="Airco DH.9">DH 9As</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westland_Wapiti" title="Westland Wapiti">Westland Wapitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hart" title="Hawker Hart">Hawker Harts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hind" title="Hawker Hind">Hawker Hind</a> light bombers. All the aircraft used a grass air strip.\n</p><p>In 1918 the Royal Air Force was formed and the airfield was named <i>RAF Turnhouse</i> and ownership transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Air_Ministry" title="Air Ministry">Air Ministry</a>.\n</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> broke out, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Fighter_Command" title="RAF Fighter Command">RAF Fighter Command</a> took control over the airfield and a runway of 3,900&#160;ft (1,189&#160;m) was paved to handle the <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Supermarine Spitfire</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/No._3_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 3 Squadron RAF">3</a>, <a href="/wiki/No._65_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 65 Squadron RAF">65</a>, and <a href="/wiki/No._141_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 141 Squadron RAF">141</a> Squadrons were present at the airbase.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_Second_World_War">Post Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Post Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When the war ended the airfield remained under military control, but by the late 1940s the first commercial services were launched. In 1947, <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a> started a service between Edinburgh and London using <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC.1_Viking" title="Vickers VC.1 Viking">Vickers Vikings</a> followed by the <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Viscount</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Vanguard" title="Vickers Vanguard">Vanguard</a> series.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1952 the runway was extended to 6000&#160;ft to handle the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Vampire" title="De Havilland Vampire">Vampire FB5s</a> operated by the resident 603 Squadron; and an aircraft arresting barrier net was installed to protect traffic on the adjacent A9 road. The net remained in place until the early 1970s and was used to stop one of the Ferranti Flying Unit Buccaneers which had over ran the runway. A further use was in 1970 when a Meteor TT20, operated by the RN Fleet Requirement Unit, overran the runway and ended up in the net. In 1956 a new passenger terminal was built to provide an improved commercial service; five years later it was extended. After the disbandment of 603 Squadron in March 1957, the Air Ministry transferred ownership to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Aviation" title="Ministry of Aviation">Ministry of Aviation</a> in 1960 to offer improved commercial service to the airport. Flying was temporarily diverted to East Fortune, which had its runway extended to accommodate the airliners of the period.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BAA_ownership_1971_to_2012">BAA ownership 1971 to 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: BAA ownership 1971 to 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_(35461420664).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg/220px-EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg/330px-EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg/440px-EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_%2835461420664%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2285" data-file-height="1550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EDI_AIRPORT_FROM_FLIGHT_ORY-KEF_757_ICELANDAIR_TF-FIK_(35461420664).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Edinburgh Airport</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg/220px-Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg/330px-Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg/440px-Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3296" data-file-height="2472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Airport_gate_lounge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">Departure gate</a> area</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/BAA_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="BAA Limited">British Airports Authority</a> took over ownership of the airport on 1 April 1971 at a time when the original terminal building was running at about eight times its design capacity. Immediate improvements to the terminal were cosmetic, such as extra seating and TV monitors for flight information, and it took two years for plans to be proposed for a completely new terminal and runway redesign. A public consultation on planning started in November 1971 and ended in February 1972. Initial stages of the redevelopment began in June 1973; they included a diversion of the River Almond. Work on the new terminal building, designed by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Matthew" title="Robert Matthew">Sir Robert Matthew</a>, started in March 1975, and the building was officially opened by Her Majesty the Queen on 27 May 1977,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> opening to the public two days later.\n</p><p>Although the original main runway 13/31 (which is now 12/30) served the airport well, its alignment (NW-SE) had the disadvantage of suffering from severe crosswinds, and the other two minor runways were very short and could not be readily extended, so movements were transferred to a new runway (07/25, which has since become 06/24) in an addition completely outside the original airfield boundary. This runway, completed in 1977, is 2,556&#160;m (8,386&#160;ft) in length, and was able to take all modern airliners including Concorde. A new terminal was built alongside the runway to cater for the additional traffic. The old terminal and hangars were converted into a cargo centre.\n</p><p>International service from Edinburgh began in 1962 with a direct service to <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, but for many years international flights were charter and private only. This started to change during the late 1970s, with direct services to continental Europe (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, 1975). By the mid-1980s direct routes included <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, but direct transatlantic flights were not yet possible as <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Prestwick_Airport" title="Glasgow Prestwick Airport">Prestwick</a> was the only "designated gateway" in Scotland under the US-UK <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_II_Agreement" title="Bermuda II Agreement">Bermuda II Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> By the time BAA had been privatised in 1987, Edinburgh Airport handled over 1.8 million passengers each year; compared to the 681,000 passengers handled in 1971 when BAA first took control of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>RAF Turnhouse was operational near the passenger terminal of the airport for all of the post war period, but was finally closed in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the original terminal upgrade in 1977, there have been major reconstructions, including extensions of the two passenger terminal aprons and a major expansion of car parking facilities, including a <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a> in 2004. In 2005, a new 57-metre-tall (187&#160;ft) air traffic control tower was completed at a cost of \xc2\xa310m. An extension to the terminal called the South East Pier opened in September 2006. This extension initially added six gates on a new pier to the south-east of the original building. A further four gates were added to the South East Pier at the end of 2008.\n</p><p>On 19 October 2011, BAA Limited announced its intention to sell the airport, following a decision by the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition Commission (United Kingdom)">Competition Commission</a> requiring BAA to sell either <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow Airport</a> or Edinburgh Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> BAA announced on 23 April 2012 that it had sold Edinburgh Airport to <a href="/wiki/Global_Infrastructure_Partners" title="Global Infrastructure Partners">Global Infrastructure Partners</a> for a price of \xc2\xa3807.2&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2013, a further extension to the passenger terminal was announced, taking the terminal building up to the Edinburgh Airport tram stop. The opening of the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Trams" title="Edinburgh Trams">Edinburgh Trams</a> in May 2014 created the first rail connection to Edinburgh Airport. Whilst the number of passengers has increased, the number of flights actually decreased in 2014 due to planes operating at higher capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Passenger traffic at Edinburgh Airport reached a record level in 2015 with over 11.1&#160;million passengers<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and over 109,000 aircraft movements.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The terminal building is currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2017)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> being expanded with an investment of \xc2\xa340m. A new \xc2\xa325m expansion project involving the construction of a new 6,000m\xc2\xb2 building, housing a security hall and retail areas, is also currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2017)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> under way at the airport. On 23 February 2016, Ryanair announced a growth of 20% in passenger numbers, bringing the airline\'s annual passenger capacity at Edinburgh Airport to 2.5 million. This was coupled with the news of six new services to Ryanair\'s winter schedule from Edinburgh, in addition to more services on its popular European destinations. In February 2016, consultancy firm Biggar Economics announced that Edinburgh Airport contributes almost \xc2\xa31 billion to the Scottish economy every year.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> As part of the expansion works, Runway 12/30 was officially withdrawn from use on 29 March 2018.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights to and from Edinburgh:<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Regional" title="Aer Lingus Regional">Aer Lingus Regional</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">Belfast\xe2\x80\x93City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cork_Airport" title="Cork Airport">Cork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/AirBaltic" title="AirBaltic">airBaltic</a> </td><td> <b>Seasonal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">Riga</a> (begins 4 June 2021)<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a> </td><td> <b>Seasonal:</b> <a class="RM_"></div>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMr" colspan="2"><div class="RMsi"><i><a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a></i></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding:0 3px 0 0;">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="padding:0 0 0 3px;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several operators provide bus services from the airport:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lothian_Buses" title="Lothian Buses">Lothian Buses</a> provides public transportation to the airport and Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/First_Scotland_East" title="First Scotland East">First</a> provides public transportation to the airport and West Lothian with one service.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_East_Scotland" title="Stagecoach East Scotland">Stagecoach</a> provides public transportation to the airport and Fife with one service.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xplore_Dundee" title="Xplore Dundee">Xplore Dundee</a> provides public transport to the airport from Dundee.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Citylink" title="Scottish Citylink">Citylink</a> provides public transportation to the airport from Glasgow and Stirling.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport lies on the <a href="/wiki/A8_road_(Scotland)" title="A8 road (Scotland)">A8 road</a>, and can be reached by the <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M8 motorway (Scotland)">M8 motorway</a> and the\n<a href="/wiki/M9_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M9 motorway (Scotland)">M9 motorway</a>. The airport is also within access from the <a href="/wiki/M90_motorway" title="M90 motorway">M90 motorway</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Queensferry_Crossing" title="Queensferry Crossing">Queensferry Crossing</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport has no dedicated railway station. However, it is served by the nearby <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Gateway_station" title="Edinburgh Gateway station">Edinburgh Gateway station</a>, which serves as an interchange with <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Trams" title="Edinburgh Trams">Edinburgh Trams</a> services to the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-opened_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opened-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The tram line also connects the airport to the nearby <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Park_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Park railway station">Edinburgh Park railway station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A more expensive <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Edinburgh Airport Rail Link">Edinburgh Airport Rail Link</a> project to provide a direct heavy rail link was cancelled in 2007 due to increasing costs.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is served by <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Trams" title="Edinburgh Trams">Edinburgh Trams</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> link. The system runs from the airport and travels across the western suburbs of Edinburgh, terminating in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trams-map_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trams-map-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:0.5em auto; font-size:95%; border-top: 0px none;">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="vertical-align: middle; width: 30%; border: 1px solid #aaa; border-left: none; border-bottom: none;">Preceding station\n</th>\n<th style="border: none; border-top: 1px solid #aaa;">&#160;\n</th>\n<th style="vertical-align: middle; border: none; border-top: 1px solid #aaa;"><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Trams" title="Edinburgh Trams">Edinburgh Trams</a>\n</th>\n<th style="border: none; border-top: 1px solid #aaa;">&#160;\n</th>\n<th style="vertical-align: middle; width: 30%; border: 1px solid #aaa; border-right: none; border-bottom: none;">Following station\n</th></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1" style="vertical-align: middle; text-align:center; border-left: 0px none; border-right: 1px #aaa solid; border-top: 1px #aaa solid; border-bottom:0px none;"><a href="/wiki/Ingliston_Park_%26_Ride_tram_stop" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingliston Park &amp; Ride tram stop">Ingliston Park &amp; Ride</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#8D122A; border-left: 0px none; border-right: 0px none; border-top:1px #aaa solid; border-bottom:0px none;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td rowspan="1" style="vertical-align: middle; text-align: center; border-left: 1px #aaa solid; border-right: 1px #aaa solid; border-top:solid 1px #aaa; border-bottom:0px none;"><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Trams" title="Edinburgh Trams">Edinburgh Trams</a><br /><small>Line 1</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#8D122A; border-left: 0px none; border-right: 0px none; border-top:1px #aaa solid; border-bottom:0px none;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td rowspan="1" style="vertical-align: middle; text-align:center; border-left: 1px #aaa solid; border-right: 0px none; border-top: 1px #aaa solid; border-bottom:0px none;"><i>Terminus </i><br />\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 20 July 1970 a <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_HS-125" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawker Siddeley HS-125">Hawker Siddeley HS-125</a>-3B (G-AXPS) operated by the Imperial Tobacco Company crashed on takeoff from Turnhouse on an empty positioning flight to Newcastle. The aircraft was a total loss and whilst the pilot was uninjured, the copilot was declared dead on arrival at hospital. The probable cause of the crash was thought to be the application of incorrect rudder following a simulated engine failure on take-off. The reason for this application of incorrect rudder has not been determined.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Moth_Minor" title="De Havilland Moth Minor">De Havilland Moth Minor</a> (G-AFOZ) crashed at Turnhouse during a low level display on 3 May 1975. One of the two occupants died in hospital the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 February 2001, a <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a> <a href="/wiki/Shorts_360" class="mw-redirect" title="Shorts 360">Shorts 360</a> (G-BNMT) operating a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mail" title="Royal Mail">Royal Mail</a> flight to <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, crashed into the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a> shortly after taking off from Edinburgh at 1730 GMT. Both crew members were killed, but there were no passengers on board. A fatal accident inquiry later blamed a buildup of <a href="/wiki/Slush_(snow)" class="mw-redirect" title="Slush (snow)">slush</a> in the aircraft\'s engines before the crash. A protective covering had not been fitted to the engine intakes while the aircraft was parked at Edinburgh for several hours in heavy snow.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edinburgh_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output
